e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-126h8e-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div data-testid="single-byline" class="ssrcss-sevsa1-ContributorContainer ee66fvo3"><div class="ssrcss-dt4z-ContributorInfo ee66fvo0"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">By</span><span class="ssrcss-nsjd43-TextContributorName epw3ir01">Emma Smith</span><div class="ssrcss-dqo7s5-ContributorDetails ee66fvo2"><span class="ssrcss-1m5444d-Text ee66fvo4">BBC Sport journalist in Milan</span></div></div></div></div></div><div data-block="metadata" class="ssrcss-l7emlr-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-126h8e-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div data-testid="metadata"><div><ul role="list" class="ssrcss-12zvu4f-MetadataStripContainer eh44mf03"><div class="ssrcss-10q9h22-GroupChildrenForWrapping eh44mf02"><li role="listitem" class="ssrcss-4l48fz-MetadataStripItem eh44mf01"><div class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Published</div><div class="ssrcss-m5j4pi-MetadataContent eh44mf00"><span class="ssrcss-1pvwv4b-MetadataSnippet e4wm5bw3"><span class="ssrcss-61mhsj-MetadataText e4wm5bw1"><time data-testid="timestamp" dateTime="2026-02-12T13:58:45.709Z">12 February 2026</time></span></span></div></li></div></ul></div></div></div></div><div data-block="text" class="ssrcss-vxwoax-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-126h8e-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div data-testid="rich-text"><div class="ssrcss-nqezkk-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><b class="ssrcss-1xjjfut-BoldText e5tfeyi3">The biggest controversy of the Milan-Cortina 2026 Winter Olympics came to a head on Thursday morning, as Ukraine&#x27;s Vladyslav Heraskevych was banned from competing.</b></p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Heraskevych, who was his country&#x27;s flagbearer at the opening ceremony, wished to compete in the men&#x27;s skeleton while wearing a special remebrance helmet featuring artwork depicting Ukrainian athletes killed during the Russian invasion.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">But the International Olympic Committee (IOC) said this contravened the Olympic charter â the rules and bylaws for the organisation of the Games â and informed him on Tuesday that he would not be allowed to compete in the helmet.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">After two days of discussions in which Heraskevych refused to back down, <a href="/sport/articles/c309pj8d8qqo" class="ssrcss-18834jl-InlineLink e1kn3p7n0">it was confirmed on Thursday morning</a> that he had been disqualified.</p></div></div></div></div><div data-block="subheadline" class="ssrcss-vxwoax-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-usmnse-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div data-testid="subheadline"><h2 id="What-has-been-the-reaction" tabindex="-1" class="ssrcss-1fbl9fk-Heading e10rt3ze0"><span role="text">What has been the reaction?</span></h2></div></div></div><div data-block="image" class="ssrcss-l7emlr-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-126h8e-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div data-testid="image" class="ssrcss-1q3np1j-StyledFigureCaption ehbdhz00"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-15twdc6-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Ukraine&#x27;s Vladyslav Heraskevych wore the helmet during his practice runs in Cortina</p></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><div data-block="text" class="ssrcss-vxwoax-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-126h8e-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div data-testid="rich-text"><div class="ssrcss-nqezkk-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The decision to disqualify Heraskevych has drawn shock and condemnation from many former and current Olympic athletes.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Lizzy Yarnold, Team GB&#x27;s two-time Olympic skeleton gold medallist, told BBC Sport: &quot;I think it is actually quite shocking. Within the sliding community there is shock and confusion.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;This [wearing the helmet] was a reaction to something which was an act of memorial and incredibly emotionally important to him.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;I think the IOC owe him an apology and this was the wrong decision.&quot;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Two-time Olympic bobsledder John Jackson was equally unimpressed with the IOC.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Jackson, who also served as a Royal Marines commando, told the BBC: &quot;His approach to that is about remembering those who have fallen.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;For me, being military and now a veteran, remembrance is really important to all veterans. We have all lost friends and colleagues in conflict, and we all know someone who isn&#x27;t here and paid the ultimate sacrifice.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;I support him in what he was trying to achieve. It is really important to remember those who have given their life for something that ultimately doesn&#x27;t need to happen.&quot;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Heraskevych meanwhile told the BBC that being banned only left him feeling &quot;emptiness.&quot;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;Yesterday and before yesterday I was training good. I could be among the medallists for this event, but suddenly because of some interpretation of the rules that I do not agree with, I am not able to compete,&quot; he said.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;Expression guidelines - what do you consider as expression? Many others here in this arena have helmets with different colours and I believe that is also a kind of expression.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;Some others had national symbols, that is also expression. For some reason, their helmets weren&#x27;t checked and they were allowed to compete but I am not.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;I believe they [those who have fallen] deserve to be here because of their sacrifice. I want to honour them and their families.&quot;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Heraskevych&#x27;s international team mates showed their support throughout Thursday&#x27;s competition in Italy.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Alpine skier Dmytro Shepiuk displayed a note reading &quot;Ukrainian heroes with us&quot; after competing, while luger Olena Smaha also voiced support for Heraskevych wearing a glove reading: &quot;Remembrance is not a violation.&quot;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Ukraine president Volodymyr Zelensky accused the IOC of &quot;playing into the hands of the Russian aggressor&quot; after Heraskevych&#x27;s disqualification</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;Sport shouldn&#x27;t mean amnesia, and the Olympic movement should help stop wars, not play into the hands of aggressors,&quot; <a href="https://x.com/ZelenskyyUa/status/2021918537271439597" class="ssrcss-18834jl-InlineLink e1kn3p7n0">he wrote on X<span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">, <!-- -->external</span></a>.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;Unfortunately, the decision of the International Olympic Committee to disqualify Ukrainian skeleton racer Vladyslav Heraskevych says otherwise.&quot;</p></div></div></div></div><div data-block="media" class="ssrcss-l7emlr-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-126h8e-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div class="ssrcss-1uy5kw5-FullWidthWrapper ep2nwvo1"><figure class="ssrcss-pqb4c0-StyledFigure class="ssrcss-nbxsk2-TextContent eitf6461"><h2 type="normal" class="ssrcss-yt0hgh-Heading e10rt3ze0">To play this video you need to enable JavaScript in your browser.</h2><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">This video can not be played</p></div></div></div></noscript></div></div><figcaption class="ssrcss-1q3np1j-StyledFigureCaption ehbdhz00"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Media caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-15twdc6-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Why IOC has banned Ukraine&#x27;s Heraskevych</p></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><div data-block="subheadline" class="ssrcss-vxwoax-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-usmnse-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div data-testid="subheadline"><h2 id="What-do-the-IOC-rules-say" tabindex="-1" class="ssrcss-1fbl9fk-Heading e10rt3ze0"><span role="text">What do the IOC rules say?</span></h2></div></div></div><div data-block="text" class="ssrcss-vxwoax-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-126h8e-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div data-testid="rich-text"><div class="ssrcss-nqezkk-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Heraskevych wore the helmet in all his training runs before the competition began and carried it through media mixed zones and in multiple interviews.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">But IOC rules dictated that he would not be allowed to wear it during official competition.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">They cited <a href="https://stillmed.olympics.com/media/Documents/International-Olympic-Committee/IOC-Publications/EN-Olympic-Charter.pdf" class="ssrcss-18834jl-InlineLink e1kn3p7n0">rule 40.2 of the Olympic Charter<span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">, <!-- -->external</span></a>, which states: &quot;All competitors, team officials or other team personnel in the Olympic Games shall enjoy freedom of expression in keeping with the Olympic values and the fundamental principles of Olympism, and in accordance with the guidelines determined by the IOC Executive Board.&quot;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">These are the <a href="https://www.olympics.com/athlete365/articles/athlete-expression/athlete-expression-guidelines-for-milano-cortina-2026" class="ssrcss-18834jl-InlineLink e1kn3p7n0">athlete expression guidelines<span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-i2z2ig-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">, <!-- -->external</span></a>, determined in 2023 and which have been codified into Olympic rules.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">This states that: &quot;The focus at the Olympic Games must remain on athletes&#x27; performances, sport and the harmony that the games seek to advance.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;It is a fundamental principle that sport at the Olympic Games is neutral and must be separate from political, religious and any other type of interference. Specifically, the focus on the field of play during competitions and official ceremonies must be on celebrating athletes&#x27; performances.&quot;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">They say athletes can express their views during Olympic Games when speaking to the media, on social media, and on the field of play at the start of competition or during their introduction.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">However, they forbid these expressions during medal ceremonies, during competition and in the Olympic village.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">If these rules are broken, participants &quot;may be subject to the IOC&#x27;s disciplinary proceedings.&quot;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The IOC said these changes have been agreed after consultation with 4,500 athletes â stating that the focus on the field of play must be on the sport.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">It was initially erroneously claimed by the IOC that it was rule 50 -  which states that &quot;no kind of demonstration or political, religious or racial propaganda is permitted in any Olympic sites&quot; - that resulted in the disqualification.</p></div></div></div></div><div data-block="image" class="ssrcss-l7emlr-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-126h8e-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div class="ssrcss-13v8d32-Placeholder etlorgc0"><picture><source srcSet="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/240/cpsprodpb/c2cf/live/f970bf80-0814-11f1-8fdd-d9a354700c27.jpg.webp 240w, e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Heraskevych&#x27;s father Mykhailo was consoled by members of other federations after the decision was made</p></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><div data-block="subheadline" class="ssrcss-vxwoax-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-usmnse-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div data-testid="subheadline"><h2 id="What-is-the-IOCs-reponse" tabindex="-1" class="ssrcss-1fbl9fk-Heading e10rt3ze0"><span role="text">What is the IOC&#x27;s reponse</span></h2></div></div></div><div data-block="text" class="ssrcss-vxwoax-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-126h8e-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div data-testid="rich-text"><div class="ssrcss-nqezkk-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">IOC president Kirsty Coventry visited Heraskevych and his father in Cortina at 7.30am on the morning of competition, to make a last-gasp plea for him to not wear the helmet.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">She said they had a lengthy, respectful meeting â but ultimately no compromise could be reached.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;No-one is disagreeing with the messaging. The messaging is a powerful message of remembrance, it&#x27;s a message of memory, and no-one is disagreeing with that,&quot; Coventry told the media.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;What I proposed to him this morning and to his dad - because he also said when he goes down it&#x27;s blurry, you can&#x27;t really see it - so I said: &#x27;Could we find a solution where we pay homage to his message, to his helmet before he races, then as soon as he&#x27;s finished racing going into the mixed zone where you can see the pictures?&#x27;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;Sadly, we&#x27;ve not been able to come to that solution. I really wanted to see him race today. It&#x27;s been an emotional morning.&quot;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Coventry was seen to be in tears after leaving the meeting. A former Olympian herself, she won two gold medals in swimming for Zimbabwe.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The IOC have also reinstated Heraskevych&#x27;s accreditation, allowing him to stay around the Games and in the Olympic village for the remainder of the competition.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In a tense media conference on Thursday morning, IOC spokesperson Mark Adams defended their decision to ban Heraskevych.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Adams said that if they allowed athletes to wear kit commemorating those killed in war, it would open the Games to exploitation.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;There are according to the Red Cross, 130 conflicts going on at any one time,&quot; he said. &quot;We can&#x27;t have them all in competition with each other at the Games.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;The field of play could become a field of expression, you could see it would lead to chaos. We cannot have athletes have pressure put on them by political masters to make expressions during competition.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;We do our best to create a level playing field, I make no apologies for that.&quot;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Adams also denied that the IOC had been pressured by the Russian Olympic Committee or government to ban Heraskevych.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Heraskevych meanwhile has made an urgent appeal against the decision to the Court of Arbitration for Sport (CAS).</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">CAS can hold ad-hoc committees during the Games, meaning his appeal will be heard immediately - although BBC Sport understands there is currently no timeframe for a decision.</p></div></div></div></div><div data-block="links" class="ssrcss-vxwoax-ComponentWrapper e1aon0op1"><div class="ssrcss-126h8e-Spacer e1aon0op0"><div spacing="4"
